Stage by Stage — Complete Detail
Stage 1: Parallel Document Workers
What They Are
Eight specialized Celery workers, each expert at reading one specific document type. They all fire simultaneously the moment documents are uploaded.

Why Parallel
Sequential processing of 8 documents at 45 seconds each is 6 minutes. Parallel processing is 45 seconds regardless of how many documents there are. The slowest worker determines total time, not the sum of all workers.

Why Specialized Workers Instead of One Generic Worker
A generic worker that tries to read every document type does every type poorly. Bank statement columns are completely different from annual report tables. GST returns have specific field names that only make sense in GST context. Board minutes are free-form prose. Each type needs different parsing logic, different extraction schemas, different validation rules. Specialization means each worker knows exactly what to look for and exactly what format to produce.

What Each Worker Does and Extracts
Worker 1: Annual Report Processor

Input: Annual Report PDF (typically 150-300 pages)

Parsing approach:
  Unstructured.io for spatial layout understanding
  Camelot for financial tables
  Tesseract if pages are scanned

What it extracts:
  Financial statements (P&L, Balance Sheet, Cash Flow)
  Notes to accounts (where the real risks hide)
  Auditor's report and qualifications
  Director's report (management commentary)
  Related party transaction disclosures
  Segment reporting
  Contingent liabilities
  Post balance sheet events

Special attention:
  Auditor qualifications → highest priority flag
  "Going concern" mention → immediate ticket
  Related party section → feed directly to Neo4j
  Contingent liabilities → feed to legal risk module

Output format:
  AnnualReportData object (Pydantic validated)
  with confidence score per field
  with source page number per field
Worker 2: Bank Statement Processor

Input: Bank statement PDF or Excel
       (multiple banks possible, multiple months)

Parsing approach:
  If Excel: Pandas direct read
  If PDF: Camelot table extraction
  Pattern matching for different bank formats
  (HDFC format ≠ SBI format ≠ ICICI format)

What it extracts:
  Monthly inflows and outflows
  Average monthly balance
  EMI/loan repayment transactions
  Large round-number transactions (fraud signal)
  Cash deposits pattern
  Cheque bounce incidents
  Overdraft utilization
  Salary credits (workforce size indicator)

Cross-check computations:
  Total annual inflows vs GST declared revenue
  Cash deposit pattern (regular cash = suspicious)
  End-of-quarter spikes (circular trading signal)
  Loan repayment regularity

Output format:
  BankStatementData object
  with monthly aggregates
  with anomaly flags pre-computed
Worker 3: GST Returns Processor

Input: GSTR-3B PDF/Excel (monthly returns)
       GSTR-2A PDF/Excel (auto-populated from supplier filings)

This is the most India-specific worker.
Requires understanding of GST filing system.

What it extracts:
  Monthly taxable turnover (GSTR-3B)
  Input tax credit claimed (GSTR-3B)
  Input tax credit actually available (GSTR-2A)
  HSN-wise sales summary
  Supplier list from GSTR-2A

Critical computation:
  GSTR-3B ITC claimed vs GSTR-2A ITC available
  Gap = potential fake ITC claims
  This is a fraud indicator specific to India

  Annual GST revenue vs bank statement inflows
  Large gap = possible revenue inflation

Output format:
  GSTData object
  with GSTR-2A vs 3B reconciliation
  with annualized revenue figure
  with ITC discrepancy flag
Worker 4: ITR Processor

Input: ITR-6 XML or PDF (company income tax return)

What it extracts:
  Schedule BP: Business income
  Schedule BS: Balance sheet as per ITR
  Depreciation schedule
  Tax paid vs refund
  Loans and advances per ITR

Why ITR matters:
  Companies sometimes show different numbers
  to the bank (higher profit = more credit)
  vs to tax department (lower profit = less tax)
  ITR is filed under penalty of law
  So ITR numbers are often more honest

Key cross-checks:
  ITR revenue vs Annual Report revenue
  ITR profit vs Annual Report profit
  Large gap between these = management risk

Output format:
  ITRData object
  with all schedules extracted
  with ITR-vs-financials gap computed
Worker 5: Legal Notice Processor

Input: Legal notices, court orders, 
       demand notices from banks/creditors

Parsing approach:
  These are often poorly formatted PDFs
  Unstructured.io for layout
  LLM extraction for semantic understanding
  (legal language needs contextual reading)

What it extracts:
  Nature of claim (debt recovery, cheque bounce,
  contract dispute, consumer complaint)
  Claimant identity
  Claim amount
  Court/authority name
  Date filed
  Current status
  Next hearing date

Why important:
  A legal notice is often the first visible sign
  of a financial dispute
  It predates court cases
  Companies don't voluntarily disclose these

Output format:
  LegalData object
  with structured case details
  with severity classification
Worker 6: Board Meeting Minutes Processor

Input: Board meeting minutes (PDF, Word, or scanned)

This worker is one of the NEW ADDITIONS
from our PS review.

Parsing approach:
  Unstructured.io for document structure
  LLM (Claude Haiku) for semantic extraction
  because minutes are free-form prose
  requiring contextual understanding

What it extracts:
  Meeting dates and attendance
  (who was present, who was absent)
  Resolutions passed
  Matters flagged as concerns
  Director dissent votes recorded
  Related party transactions approved
  Capital expenditure decisions
  Loan discussions and approvals
  Any mention of financial difficulty
  Management plans discussed vs results

Why board minutes are gold:
  Board discusses problems BEFORE they
  appear in public documents
  A director raising concerns 6 months before
  a financial crisis is an early warning signal
  Related party transactions approved in minutes
  can be cross-referenced with what's declared
  in annual report — gap = concealment

Special detection:
  "Going concern" discussions
  Director resignation preceded by dissent votes
  Auditor concerns raised in board
  Delayed audit completion discussions

Output format:
  BoardMinutesData object
  with timeline of key decisions
  with concern flags
  with related party approvals list
Worker 7: Shareholding Pattern Processor

Input: Shareholding pattern disclosure
       (quarterly filing with BSE/NSE if listed,
        or provided by company if unlisted)

This worker is another NEW ADDITION
from our PS review.

What it extracts:
  Promoter holding percentage
  Promoter share pledge percentage
    (THIS IS CRITICAL — high pledge = distress)
  Public/institutional holding
  FII/FPI holding
    (foreign institutional confidence indicator)
  DII holding (domestic institutional)
  Top 10 shareholders
  Cross-holdings with related entities

Why shareholding matters:
  If promoter has pledged 70%+ of shares:
    → They borrowed against their own shares
    → They are personally financially distressed
    → If stock falls, lender sells pledged shares
    → Promoter loses control → company instability
    → This is a massive hidden risk

  Cross-holdings reveal:
    Company A holds 15% of Company B
    Company B holds 12% of Company A
    → Circular ownership = related parties
    → Board decisions are not independent

Output format:
  ShareholdingData object
  with pledge percentage prominently flagged
  with cross-holding graph data for Neo4j
Worker 8: Rating Report Processor

Input: CRISIL / ICRA / CARE / India Ratings report

This worker is another NEW ADDITION
from our PS review.

Parsing approach:
  These are structured PDFs with consistent format
  Unstructured.io + targeted extraction

What it extracts:
  Current rating (e.g., BBB+)
  Rating outlook (Stable / Negative / Watch)
  Previous rating (was it downgraded?)
  Rationale summary
  Key rating drivers (positive and negative)
  Rating sensitivities (what would change it)
  Liquidity assessment
  Industry comparison
  Financial ratios as assessed by agency

Why rating reports matter:
  Rating agencies have information banks don't
  They meet management, access internal financials
  A "Rating Watch Negative" is 6-month advance notice
  Their risk articulation is professionally written
    → Can be directly used in CAM sections
  Downgrade history = repeated financial stress

Special detection:
  Watch Negative + Stable outlook = imminent downgrade
  Two-notch downgrade in 12 months = severe stress
  "Stretched liquidity" language = cash flow problem
  "Weak debt coverage" = DSCR issue

Output format:
  RatingReportData object
  with rating history timeline
  with key concern extraction
  with liquidity assessment
Technology Stack for Workers
Celery — Task queue system. Each document becomes a Celery task. Tasks are distributed across multiple workers automatically. If a worker crashes, Celery reassigns the task. You can monitor all tasks in real time. The specific reason Celery over alternatives: it integrates natively with Redis, it's the Python standard for distributed task processing, and it gives you real-time task status that feeds the progress bar in the UI.

Redis — Two roles for workers: the task queue (Celery uses Redis as its broker) and the staging area (each worker writes its completed output to a Redis key that Agent 0.5 monitors). Why Redis as staging area? Because it's already there for Celery, it supports key-based existence checks (Agent 0.5 polls for all keys being present), and it's fast enough for the small JSON payloads workers produce.

Unstructured.io — The core parsing library for complex PDFs. The critical advantage over PyMuPDF or pdfplumber is spatial layout understanding. Unstructured.io knows the difference between a header, a footnote, a table cell, and body text. It reconstructs multi-column layouts correctly. For scanned documents, it integrates OCR automatically. For Indian annual reports which are notoriously complex multi-column layouts with tables spanning pages, this is non-negotiable.

Tesseract OCR — For pages identified as scanned images. Configured with page-level parallelism: a 100-page scanned document is split into 100 individual images, all processed simultaneously across Celery workers. Total OCR time for 100 pages drops from 3 minutes to under 30 seconds.

Camelot — Specifically for extracting tables from PDFs. Regular text extraction destroys table structure. Camelot understands table boundaries, column alignments, and merged cells. Critical for financial statements where numbers are in tables and the column header tells you what the number means.

Pandas + OpenPyXL — For Excel and CSV inputs (bank statements, GST returns often come as Excel). Pandas reads them directly into structured DataFrames. OpenPyXL handles formula-heavy Excel files that Pandas alone can't parse.

Claude Haiku — Used specifically by the Board Minutes and Legal Notice workers where semantic understanding is required. Haiku is chosen over Sonnet here because these extractions are relatively structured — extract specific fields from prose — and Haiku is 5x faster and 10x cheaper while being sufficient for structured extraction tasks.

Pydantic v2 — Each worker produces a typed, validated output object. If an annual report extraction produces a string where a float is expected, Pydantic catches it before the bad data propagates. Each document type has its own Pydantic model (AnnualReportData, BankStatementData, GSTData etc.) with field-level validation rules.

Stage 2: Agent 0.5 — The Consolidator
What It Does
Waits for all parallel workers to complete, then produces a single unified RawDataPackage.

The Complete Internal Flow
AGENT 0.5 INTERNAL PIPELINE

Step 1: Completion Monitor
        ─────────────────
        Poll Redis staging area
        Check all expected worker keys present
        
        If a worker hasn't finished in 5 minutes:
          → Timeout flag raised
          → Partial processing option offered to user
          → "Bank statement still processing.
             Continue without it (lower confidence)
             or wait?"

Step 2: Schema Normalization
        ──────────────────────
        Each worker produced its own typed object.
        Agent 0.5 maps all of them to a unified schema.
        
        AnnualReportData.revenue_fy24 → UnifiedData.revenue.fy24
        ITRData.schedule_bp_income    → UnifiedData.revenue.itr_fy24
        GSTData.annual_turnover       → UnifiedData.revenue.gst_fy24
        BankData.total_annual_inflows → UnifiedData.revenue.bank_fy24
        
        Now all revenue figures are in one place
        with their source labels.

Step 3: Conflict Detection Engine
        ───────────────────────────
        For every field that multiple sources provide:
        
        Revenue FY2024:
          Annual Report says: ₹124.5 crore
          ITR says:           ₹98.2 crore
          GST says:           ₹118.7 crore
          Bank inflows:       ₹71.4 crore
          
          Are all within 5% of each other? → Accept highest confidence
          Is there a gap > 10%? → Raise conflict flag
          Is one source government-filed? → That source gets priority
          
        The priority hierarchy:
          Government filings (ITR, GST) > Third-party (Bank) > Self-reported (Annual Report)
          More recent > Older
          More specific > Aggregate
          
        When priority doesn't resolve:
          Store all values with source labels
          Mark field as CONFLICTED
          Raise immediate ticket
          Block this field from scoring until resolved

Step 4: Completeness Check
        ──────────────────
        Required fields check:
        
        MANDATORY (block if missing):
          → Revenue for at least 2 years
          → DSCR-computable data (EBITDA + debt service)
          → Bank statement for at least 6 months
          → GST returns for at least 12 months
          
        IMPORTANT (warn if missing, proceed with flag):
          → ITR (proceed but flag confidence reduction)
          → Rating report (proceed, note absence)
          → Board minutes (proceed, note absence)
          
        OPTIONAL (note absence only):
          → Shareholding pattern
          → Additional legal notices
          
        For each missing mandatory field:
          → Pipeline pauses
          → User notified with specific request
          → "GST returns for Q3 FY2024 not found.
             Please upload to proceed."

Step 5: Cross-Document Contradiction Detection
        ─────────────────────────────────────────
        This is the most important step.
        
        Looks for contradictions ACROSS document types:
        
        Check 1: Litigation disclosure
          Annual Report: "No pending litigation"
          Legal Notice worker: Found 2 cases
          Board Minutes: Discussed ongoing dispute
          → CONTRADICTION ticket raised immediately
          → Severity: HIGH
        
        Check 2: Financial consistency
          Annual Report profit: ₹8.2 crore
          ITR income: ₹3.1 crore
          → Gap > 60% → CONFLICT ticket
          → Could be legitimate (timing differences)
          → Or could be dual accounting (fraud)
        
        Check 3: Related party consistency
          Annual Report related party section: 
            "Transactions with 2 related parties"
          Board Minutes: "Approved transactions with 
            5 related entities this year"
          → Undisclosed related parties detected
          → HIGH priority ticket
        
        Check 4: Director information
          Annual Report directors list: 4 directors
          Shareholding pattern: 3 directors
          → Board change not reflected → flag
        
        Check 5: Pledging vs financial health claim
          Annual Report: "Company in strong financial position"
          Shareholding pattern: 72% promoter shares pledged
          → Management narrative vs actual financial behavior
          → Ticket raised: "Management claims health
             contradicted by 72% pledge ratio"

Step 6: Build RawDataPackage
        ─────────────────────
        Single unified object with:
          → All fields from all workers
          → Conflict markers where they exist
          → Missing field markers where applicable
          → Cross-document contradictions flagged
          → Every field tagged with its source document
          → Confidence score per field
          → All tickets raised logged within the package
Technologies Inside Agent 0.5
Redis Pub/Sub + Polling — Agent 0.5 subscribes to a Redis channel. Each worker publishes a "done" message when complete. Agent 0.5 listens and tracks completion status. When all required workers publish done, it proceeds. This is cleaner than polling and more responsive.

Python asyncio — Agent 0.5 itself runs asynchronously. While waiting for the last few workers, it can already start processing the completed ones — pre-normalizing their outputs, pre-running conflict checks on the data that's already arrived. This overlaps waiting time with processing time.

Pydantic v2 with discriminated unions — The unified RawDataPackage model uses Pydantic's discriminated union feature to handle fields that might come from different sources with different confidence levels. Each field is not just a value but a SourcedValue object:

class SourcedValue:
    value: float
    source: str
    source_document: str
    page_number: int
    confidence: float
    conflicts: list[ConflictRecord]
LangChain Claude Haiku — For the cross-document contradiction detection step. Some contradictions are obvious (two different numbers for the same metric). But some require semantic understanding ("no pending litigation" vs a board minutes discussion of "ongoing disputes with counterparties"). Haiku reads both passages and determines if they contradict each other semantically.

PostgreSQL — Agent 0.5 writes its conflict log and contradiction records to PostgreSQL immediately. This creates a permanent record that the ticketing system can reference and that audit trails require.

Stage 3: The Validator
What It Does
Receives the RawDataPackage from Agent 0.5 and makes a binary decision: is this data good enough to proceed?

Validation Checks
CHECK 1: Schema completeness
  Are all mandatory Pydantic fields populated?
  Are all field types correct?
  Are all numerical ranges sensible?
  (Revenue cannot be negative. 
   DSCR cannot be 1000x.
   Dates cannot be in the future.)

CHECK 2: Mandatory document presence
  Are all required document types present?
  At least 2 years of financial data?
  Bank statements covering > 6 months?

CHECK 3: Conflict resolution status
  Are there unresolved HARD conflicts?
  (A hard conflict blocks the pipeline)
  Are there open mandatory tickets?

CHECK 4: Data recency
  Is the most recent data within 18 months?
  (Older data means assessment is unreliable)

CHECK 5: GSTIN verification
  Cross-reference submitted GSTIN against
  live GST portal to confirm it's real
  and matches the company name

OUTCOMES:
  All pass → proceed to Agent 1.5
  Missing documents → pause, request from user
  Unresolvable conflict → escalate to senior manager
  GSTIN mismatch → immediate fraud flag
Technologies
Pydantic v2 — The primary validation engine. The entire RawDataPackage schema is defined in Pydantic. Validation is instantaneous and produces precise error messages that tell the user exactly what is missing and why.

GSTIN Verifier — Direct API call to the government GST portal. Verifies the GSTIN number is real, active, and belongs to the stated company name. This is the first hard anti-fraud check — document fabrication often involves creating fake GST summaries with real-looking but invalid GSTINs.

LangGraph interrupt node — If the validator finds missing mandatory documents, it uses LangGraph's interrupt mechanism to pause the pipeline and send a structured request to the UI. The credit officer sees exactly what is needed. The pipeline resumes automatically when the additional documents are uploaded.

Stage 4: Agent 1.5 — The Organizer
What It Does
Takes the validated RawDataPackage and transforms it into a fully structured, computed, tagged OrganizedPackage. This is the last purely internal processing step before external research begins.

The Complete Internal Flow
AGENT 1.5 INTERNAL PIPELINE

Step 1: Map to 5 Cs Structure
        ───────────────────────
        Every piece of data gets assigned to its
        position in the 5 Cs framework.
        
        This is not just labeling. It means:
        
        CHARACTER bucket receives:
          → Promoter identity (from annual report)
          → Director list (from annual report + shareholding)
          → SEBI history (will be added by Agent 2)
          → Board minutes governance signals
          → Management interview responses
        
        CAPACITY bucket receives:
          → Revenue 3 years (annual report + ITR + GST)
          → EBITDA computation
          → DSCR computation
          → Working capital cycle
          → Cash flow from operations
        
        CAPITAL bucket receives:
          → Net worth
          → Debt-equity ratio
          → Existing loan obligations from bank statement
          → Contingent liabilities from annual report notes
        
        COLLATERAL bucket receives:
          → Fixed assets schedule
          → Property valuations mentioned
          → Charge creation records (from MCA21 later)
        
        CONDITIONS bucket receives:
          → Industry segment
          → Sector from annual report
          → Rating report industry assessment
          → (External sector data added by Agent 2)

Step 2: Compute All Derived Metrics
        ──────────────────────────────
        All financial ratios computed ONCE here.
        Never recomputed by any downstream agent.
        Every computation tagged with formula and sources.
        
        DSCR:
          Formula: EBITDA / Total Debt Service
          EBITDA: Revenue - COGS - OpEx + Depreciation
          Debt Service: Principal repayments + Interest
          Source: Annual Report pg 67 + pg 89
          Result: 1.43x
          Confidence: 0.94
        
        Current Ratio:
          Formula: Current Assets / Current Liabilities
          Source: Balance Sheet pg 58
          Result: 1.67x
          Confidence: 0.97
        
        Debt-Equity Ratio:
          Formula: Total Debt / Net Worth
          Source: Balance Sheet pg 58
          Result: 2.1x
          Confidence: 0.97
        
        Working Capital Cycle:
          Formula: Debtor Days + Inventory Days - Creditor Days
          Source: Balance Sheet + P&L pg 58-62
          Result: 94 days
          Confidence: 0.91
        
        Revenue CAGR (3-year):
          Formula: (FY24/FY22)^(1/2) - 1
          Source: Annual Report pg 43
          Result: 18.2%
          Confidence: 0.97
        
        GST-Bank Divergence Ratio:
          Formula: GST Revenue / Bank Inflows
          GST Revenue: ₹118.7cr (from GST worker)
          Bank Inflows: ₹71.4cr (from bank worker)
          Result: 1.66x
          Flag threshold: > 1.5x is suspicious
          Flag raised: YES (1.66x)
        
        ITR-Annual Report Divergence:
          ITR Income: ₹98.2cr
          AR Revenue: ₹124.5cr
          Gap: 21%
          Flag threshold: > 10% warrants investigation
          Flag raised: YES

Step 3: Board Minutes Deep Analysis
        ─────────────────────────────
        This is a NEW FEATURE from PS review.
        
        Board minutes are processed by LLM specifically:
        
        Timeline extraction:
          Build chronological timeline of key decisions
          "March 2023 board: Discussed working capital pressure"
          "August 2023 board: CFO resignation accepted"
          "January 2024 board: New credit line approved"
        
        Concern pattern detection:
          Any "going concern" discussion → CRITICAL flag
          Repeated discussions of same problem → trend flag
          Director absence pattern → governance flag
          (Director X absent from 4 of 6 meetings = disengaged)
        
        Approval vs disclosure gap:
          Related party transactions approved in board
          Cross-reference with annual report disclosures
          Gap = undisclosed related party transactions
        
        Forward-looking statement extraction:
          What did management promise in board meeting?
          Did results match those promises?
          Consistent failure to deliver = reliability discount

Step 4: Shareholding Pattern Analysis
        ──────────────────────────────
        Another NEW FEATURE from PS review.
        
        Pledge ratio computation:
          Pledged shares / Total promoter shares
          > 50% = significant concern
          > 70% = major red flag
          > 90% = near-distress signal
        
        Holding trend analysis:
          Has promoter been reducing holding over quarters?
          Promoter selling = loss of confidence in own company
        
        Institutional holding interpretation:
          FII presence = global institutional confidence
          FII exit over quarters = international concern
          DII entry while FII exits = different risk views
        
        Cross-holding mapping:
          Any entity holding > 5% identified
          Feed to Neo4j as SHAREHOLDING relationship
          Agent 2.5 will check if these are related parties

Step 5: Build Internal Neo4j Graph
        ──────────────────────────────
        This is the internal knowledge graph built
        purely from company's own documents.
        
        Entity types extracted:
          Companies (borrower + subsidiaries + associates)
          People (promoters + directors + KMPs)
          Banks (existing lending relationships)
          Courts (from legal notices)
          Assets (properties, machinery, investments)
          Transactions (significant ones from bank + GST)
        
        Relationship types mapped:
          (Person)─[IS_DIRECTOR_OF]─▶(Company)
          (Person)─[IS_PROMOTER_OF]─▶(Company)
          (Company)─[HAS_SUBSIDIARY]─▶(Company)
          (Company)─[HAS_CUSTOMER]─▶(Company)
          (Company)─[HAS_SUPPLIER]─▶(Company)
          (Company)─[HAS_LOAN_FROM]─▶(Bank)
          (Company)─[OWNS_ASSET]─▶(Asset)
          (Company)─[IS_DEFENDANT_IN]─▶(Case)
          (Person)─[HAS_SHAREHOLDING: %]─▶(Company)
          (Person)─[PLEDGED_SHARES: %]─▶(Company)
          (Company)─[APPROVED_RPT]─▶(RelatedParty)
        
        This graph is INTERNAL ONLY at this stage.
        Agent 2 will enrich it with external nodes.
        Agent 2.5 will reason over the complete graph.

Step 6: Run ML Anomaly Suite
        ──────────────────────
        Three models run simultaneously:
        
        DOMINANT GNN:
          Input: The internal Neo4j graph
          Looks for: Circular trading subgraphs
                     Shell company cluster patterns
                     Director overlap anomalies
          Output: Fraud probability per detected pattern
          
        Isolation Forest:
          Input: Feature table of financial ratios
                 (DSCR, D/E, WC cycle, GST divergence,
                  ITR gap, revenue growth, margins)
          Looks for: Statistical outliers vs Indian
                     industry norms
          Output: Anomaly score per metric (0-1)
          
        FinBERT:
          Input: All text from annual report narrative
                 + board minutes + director's report
          Looks for: Positive language masking negatives
                     Standard risk disclosure language
                     vs genuine concern language
          Output: Buried risk score per paragraph
                  Top 5 highest-risk paragraphs flagged

Step 7: Produce FeatureObject and OrganizedPackage
        ────────────────────────────────────────────
        FeatureObject: Versioned, stored in PostgreSQL
        Contains: All computed metrics + ML scores
        
        OrganizedPackage: Comprehensive structured object
        Contains: FeatureObject + 5 Cs mapped data
                  + Neo4j graph reference + all sources
        
        Passed to Agent 2 as context for research.
Technologies Inside Agent 1.5
spaCy + GLiNER — Named entity recognition for extracting company names, people, monetary amounts, dates, and court references from document text. GLiNER is specifically chosen because it works zero-shot — it can recognize Indian company name patterns and Indian court names without needing fine-tuning. Standard NER models trained on Western text miss Indian entity patterns.

DOMINANT GNN — Graph Neural Network pre-trained on financial transaction graphs. Fine-tuned on SEBI enforcement orders describing circular trading. Takes the Neo4j graph structure as input and classifies subgraphs as fraudulent or normal. This is the best available open-source tool for exactly this problem — detecting fraud in financial graph structures.

Isolation Forest — Unsupervised anomaly detection from scikit-learn. No training data needed — it learns the distribution of normal financial ratios from the data it sees and flags statistical outliers. Lightweight, fast, and specifically designed for anomaly detection rather than classification.

FinBERT — BERT pre-trained on financial news and earnings calls by ProsusAI. Available on HuggingFace. Understands financial euphemisms. Fine-tuned additionally on SEBI downgrade reports and ICRA credit watch reports to understand Indian financial risk language specifically.

sentence-transformers/all-MiniLM-L6-v2 — Local embedding generation. All document chunks embedded locally. 25x faster than OpenAI API, zero cost, works offline. Quality is 90% of OpenAI embeddings for retrieval tasks — sufficient for all our use cases.

Neo4j Python Driver (async) — Asynchronous Neo4j writes. The graph is built while other processing continues. By the time Agent 2 needs it, the internal graph is already populated. Zero wait time added to the pipeline for graph construction.

PyTorch Geometric — The library that runs DOMINANT GNN. Handles graph-structured tensor operations. Converts Neo4j subgraphs into tensor format for GNN processing.

Stage 5: Agent 2 — The Research Agent
What It Does
Goes outside the company's own documents and finds everything the internet, government databases, and regulatory portals know about the company, its promoters, its sector, and its legal standing.

The Five Research Tracks
All five tracks fire simultaneously. Total research time is the time of the slowest single search, not the sum.

Track 1: Tavily API

Purpose: General web + financial news
Why Tavily specifically:
  Purpose-built for AI agents
  Returns clean structured text not raw HTML
  Supports domain filtering
    → Prioritize sebi.gov.in, rbi.org.in
  Has search depth control
    → search_depth="advanced" goes deep into pages
  Native LangChain tool integration
  Source credibility scoring built in

Searches fired:
  "{company} news India 2024 2025"
  "{company} {promoter_name} background"
  "{company} financial performance"
  "{company} order book contracts"
  "{company} {sector} market position"
Track 2: Exa Neural Search

Purpose: Semantic / conceptual research
Why Exa specifically:
  Neural search finds conceptually related content
  not just keyword matches
  Discovers the promoter's OTHER company default
  even if the current company is never mentioned
  Finds patterns not findable by keyword search

Searches fired:
  Semantic: "companies similar to {company} 
             that defaulted in steel sector"
  Semantic: "{promoter_name} business history"
  Semantic: "{company} related entities network"
Track 3: SerpAPI

Purpose: Indian news coverage
Why SerpAPI:
  Wraps Google search with clean JSON output
  Google has the deepest Indian news index
  Covers Economic Times, Business Standard,
  Mint, Financial Express, MoneyControl
  Regional business news not in other indexes

Searches fired:
  "{company} site:economictimes.com"
  "{company} site:livemint.com"
  "{promoter_name} news"
  "{sector} industry outlook India 2025"
  "{sector} RBI regulations 2024 2025"
Track 4: India-Specific Scrapers

These are the most valuable research components and the ones no other team will build:

MCA21 Scraper:
  Input: Company name or CIN number
  
  Fetches:
    → All current directors with DIN numbers
    → Director appointment and resignation dates
    → ALL other companies each director is/was
       director of (this is the shell company detector)
    → Registered charges (all existing loans secured
       against company assets)
    → ROC annual filing dates
       (late filings = governance problem)
    → Registered address history
       (frequent changes = shell company behavior)
    → Paid-up capital history
  
  Writes directly to Neo4j:
    For every director found:
      (Director)─[IS_DIRECTOR_OF]─▶(XYZ Steel)
    For every other company that director directs:
      (Director)─[IS_DIRECTOR_OF]─▶(Supplier A)
    For every registered charge:
      (XYZ Steel)─[HAS_CHARGE]─▶(Bank Name)
      with amount and date
  
  Why this is gold:
    Circular trading requires related parties.
    Related parties share directors.
    This scraper finds ALL director overlaps.
    Cross-referencing with supplier list from
    GST returns immediately shows related-party
    supplier relationships.

NJDG Scraper (eCourts):
  Input: Company name + state
  
  Fetches:
    → All pending civil cases
    → All disposed cases (recent 5 years)
    → Case type (recovery, cheque bounce, contract)
    → Claimant identity
    → Claim amounts
    → Court name
    → Filing date
    → Next hearing date
    → Last order summary
  
  Why comprehensive:
    Tavily will find cases reported in news.
    NJDG finds EVERY case including ones
    never reported in media.
    A ₹2cr cheque bounce case in a district court
    will never appear in any news API.
    NJDG finds it.

SEBI Scraper:
  Input: Company name + promoter names
  
  Fetches:
    → Enforcement orders
    → Adjudication orders
    → Consent orders
    → Show cause notices
    → Debarment orders
  
  Significance:
    SEBI actions indicate capital market fraud,
    insider trading, disclosure violations.
    These are about the CHARACTER of the promoter.
    Many banks miss this because it requires
    specifically checking the SEBI database.

RBI Defaulter Scraper:
  Input: Company name
  
  Fetches:
    → Wilful defaulter status
    → Defaulted amount
    → Bank(s) with whom defaulted
    → Date of classification
  
  This is a HARD BLOCK trigger.
  If found → auto-reject regardless of score.
  RBI publishes quarterly lists.
  Our scraper checks the most recent list.

GSTIN Verifier:
  Input: GSTIN number from submitted documents
  
  Verifies:
    → GSTIN exists and is active
    → Registered company name matches
    → Filing frequency (are they filing regularly?)
    → Registration date (when did they register?)
    → Cancellation status
  
  Anti-fabrication check:
    A company can submit a fake GST return PDF.
    They cannot fake what the GST portal says.
    This check catches document fabrication.
Track 5: Regulatory Intelligence

Daily crawler feeds Elasticsearch 
regulatory_watchlist index:
  RBI circulars and notifications
  SEBI regulations and amendments
  MCA notifications
  GST council decisions
  PLI scheme updates
  Sector-specific ministry notifications

When company sector is identified:
  Query: "regulations affecting {sector} 
          published in last 6 months"
  Returns: All regulatory changes that
           affect this company's operating
           environment
  
  Example for steel sector:
    "BIS quality norms tightened for 
     structural steel — October 2024"
    "Anti-dumping duty on Chinese steel 
     extended — November 2024"
    "Steel sector PLI targets revised — 2025"
Verification Engine
Every research finding passes through the verification engine before being used:

TIER CLASSIFICATION:
  Tier 1 (1.0): Government portals — treat as fact
  Tier 2 (0.85): Reputable financial media
  Tier 3 (0.60): General news, regional media
  Tier 4 (0.30): Blogs, unverified sites
  Tier 5 (0.0): Rejected — social media, anonymous

RELEVANCE SCORING:
  Entity match: Is this actually about this company?
  Temporal match: Is this recent enough to matter?
  Risk materiality: Does this affect any of the 5 Cs?

CROSS-VERIFICATION:
  Same claim from 2+ independent sources → boost confidence
  Conflicting claims from same tier → raise conflict ticket

FINAL CLASSIFICATION:
  Verified (used in scoring with citation)
  Uncertain (shown with caveat, not scored)
  Rejected (shown with reason why rejected)
  Conflicting (shown, needs human resolution)
Technologies Inside Agent 2
Tavily API — AI-native search, clean output, domain filtering, LangChain native integration.

Exa API — Neural semantic search, finds conceptually related content beyond keywords.

SerpAPI — Google wrapper for Indian news coverage.

BeautifulSoup + Selenium — Powers the five custom scrapers. BeautifulSoup for simple HTML parsing. Selenium for dynamic JavaScript-rendered pages that BeautifulSoup can't handle (some government portals render data via JavaScript).

Redis Cache — 7-day TTL per research query. If the same company was researched recently, all cached results are served instantly. Cross-company sector research is also cached — if two steel companies are assessed in the same week, the sector research is shared.

FinBERT — Scores the sentiment and risk content of every news article and research finding. Classifies each finding's risk relevance and severity level.

asyncio — All five research tracks and all individual searches within each track run as async coroutines. Maximum parallelism with minimum overhead.

Neo4j async driver — External entities and relationships are written to Neo4j asynchronously as they're discovered. By the time Agent 2.5 needs the complete graph, all external nodes are already populated.

Stage 6: Agent 2.5 — The Graph Reasoning Agent
What It Does
Takes the complete Neo4j knowledge graph — built from internal documents by Agent 1.5 and enriched with external data by Agent 2 — and runs five structured reasoning passes to find compound insights that no individual data point would reveal.

Why This Agent Is Necessary
The key insight: dangerous situations in credit are almost never found in a single data point. They emerge from the relationship between data points. Agent 2.5 is the only component that looks at the whole picture simultaneously.

The Five Reasoning Passes
Pass 1: Contradiction Detection

What it looks for:
  Facts from one source that directly contradict
  facts from another source about the same thing.

Method:
  For every factual claim in the graph:
    Find all other nodes that make a claim about
    the same entity and attribute.
    Apply semantic similarity to check if they
    agree or contradict.

Examples found:
  "No litigation" (Annual Report) 
  vs Active NJDG case
  → HIGH severity contradiction
  
  "All related party transactions disclosed"
  (Annual Report)
  vs Board minutes approval of 5 RPTs,
  annual report only shows 2
  → HIGH severity contradiction
  
  "Company in strong financial position"
  (Director's report)
  vs 72% promoter share pledge
  (Shareholding pattern)
  → MEDIUM severity contradiction
  (narrative vs behavior)

Output per contradiction:
  Both claims with exact sources
  Confidence in each claim
  Possible explanations
  Score impact
  Ticket raised with evidence attached
Pass 2: Cascade Risk Detection

What it looks for:
  Chain reactions — if entity X experiences
  a negative event, what is the downstream
  impact on the borrower?

Method:
  Multi-hop graph traversal starting from
  any node with a negative signal.
  Follow edges back to the borrower.
  Compute financial impact at each hop.

Example:
  Greenfield Energy → NCLT_INSOLVENCY status
  
  Hop 1: Greenfield is CUSTOMER_OF XYZ Steel
         Revenue dependency: 38%
         
  Hop 2: XYZ Steel has OUTSTANDING_RECEIVABLE
         from Greenfield: ₹14.2cr (180 days)
         
  Hop 3: XYZ Steel DSCR_DEPENDS_ON this revenue
         Without Greenfield: DSCR 1.43x → 1.21x
         
  Hop 4: XYZ Steel LOAN_REPAYMENT_SCHEDULE requires
         minimum DSCR 1.2x per loan covenant
         
  Final: DSCR approaches covenant breach threshold
  Cascade severity: CRITICAL

Output:
  Complete chain visualization
  Probability of cascade occurring
  Financial impact quantification
  Score impact
  CAM language prepared
Pass 3: Hidden Relationship Detection

What it looks for:
  Undisclosed connections between the borrower
  and its supposedly independent counterparties.

Method:
  Community detection algorithm on Neo4j graph.
  Find clusters of entities that are more
  connected to each other than to the rest of
  the graph.

MCA21 director network analysis:
  For every supplier, customer, and related entity:
    Check if any director of that entity is also:
      Director of borrower company
      Related person to borrower director
      Employee of borrower group
  
  Example found:
    XYZ Steel Promoter: Rajesh Shah
    Supplier A Director: Rajesh Shah (same DIN)
    Supplier B Director: Priya Shah
    Priya Shah = wife of Rajesh Shah (public records)
    Supplier C registered address = XYZ Steel office
    Supplier D: incorporated 3 months before 
                first invoice to XYZ Steel
    
    DOMINANT GNN score: 0.84 probability
    circular trading pattern
    
    Community detection confirms: these 4 entities
    form a tightly connected cluster with the
    borrower at center

Output:
  Network visualization description
  All connected entities listed
  Evidence for each connection
  Transaction amounts flowing through network
  Score impact
Pass 4: Temporal Pattern Analysis

What it looks for:
  Multi-year trends across financial, operational,
  and governance metrics that individually look
  acceptable but together show deterioration.

Method:
  For each metric with historical data points:
    Compute year-over-year change
    Compute 3-year trend direction
    Compute rate of deterioration
  
  Cross-metric correlation:
    Are multiple metrics deteriorating simultaneously?
    Is there a timeline event that explains a shift?
    (e.g., all metrics worsen after a specific quarter)

Example found:
  FY22 → FY23 → FY24 pattern:
  
  DSCR:              2.1x → 1.6x → 1.3x
  Working capital:   45d → 67d → 94d
  Current ratio:     2.1 → 1.9 → 1.67
  Gross margin:      18% → 16% → 14%
  Director changes:  None → CFO left → 2 IDs left
  
  Trend computation:
  DSCR declining at 0.4x per year
  Projected FY25: 0.9x (below 1.0x threshold)
  
  Event correlation:
  All metrics begin worsening from Q3 FY23
  Board minutes Q2 FY23: "Greenfield Energy
  payment delays discussed"
  → Single customer stress causing multi-metric
    deterioration

Output:
  Timeline of deterioration
  Projected future values
  Root cause hypothesis
  Months until critical threshold breached
  Score impact
Pass 5: Positive Signal Amplification

What it looks for:
  Genuine strengths that should reduce the
  risk score — not just absence of negatives
  but actual positive credit signals.

Method:
  Specific graph patterns known to indicate
  credit strength:
    Strong diversified order book
    Government scheme beneficiary (PLI, etc.)
    Collateral coverage significantly > 1x
    Clean promoter record over long period
    Institutional investor backing

Example found:
  Order book: ₹280cr confirmed orders
    Source: Management note + corroborated by
    customer announcement (ET article)
    Significance: 2.8x annual revenue visibility
    Score: +15 pts
  
  PLI scheme: ₹12cr annual subsidy confirmed
    Source: Ministry of Steel notification
    Significance: Government-backed cash flow
    Score: +8 pts
  
  Collateral: Factory land ₹85cr (HDFC valuation)
    vs loan ask ₹50cr
    Coverage ratio: 1.7x
    Score: +12 pts

Output:
  All genuine strengths documented with sources
  Why each is a genuine positive vs just PR
  Score impact
The Insight Store
All five passes write their outputs to the PostgreSQL Insight Store:

Table: compound_insights
  company_id, type, severity, title,
  insight_text, evidence (JSON array of sources),
  score_impact, neo4j_path_ids, confidence,
  reasoning_trace, created_at

Table: reasoning_audit_log
  Every traversal step logged
  Every pattern checked (including dismissed ones)
  Full explainability trail
Technologies Inside Agent 2.5
Neo4j with Cypher queries — All five passes are implemented as Cypher graph queries. The power of Cypher is that relationship traversal is natural — "find all nodes connected to this node through these relationship types" is one Cypher statement.

Microsoft GraphRAG — Integrated to enable the LLM to reason over the graph without seeing raw Cypher. GraphRAG creates a hierarchical summary of the graph at different levels of abstraction. The LLM can ask "what are the major risk clusters in this graph?" and GraphRAG retrieves the relevant subgraph for context.

NetworkX — Python graph analysis library. Used for community detection algorithms (Louvain method for finding tightly connected clusters). Neo4j stores the graph. NetworkX runs algorithms over it. This separation means you use each tool for what it does best.

Claude Haiku — For Pass 1 (contradiction detection) and Pass 5 (positive signal analysis) where semantic understanding of text is needed. Haiku is sufficient for these structured analysis tasks and is fast enough to run multiple passes without becoming a bottleneck.

Stage 7: Evidence Package Builder
What It Does
Takes everything from all previous stages and organizes it into one perfectly structured, fully cited package. Agent 3 reads only this package. It never touches raw documents, never queries Neo4j, never touches the Insight Store directly. The Evidence Package Builder is the last intelligence step. Agent 3 is purely a writer.

The Package Structure
EVIDENCE PACKAGE
━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━━

For each of the 5 Cs:
  
  C: CHARACTER
  ──────────────
  
  Claim: "Promoter Rajesh Shah has 22 years 
          in steel sector with clean exit history"
  Evidence:
    Source 1: MCA21 director record
              DIN 01234567, first directorship 2003
    Source 2: Business Standard profile, 2019
              "Shah Steel Components sold to Tata 2009"
    Source 3: NSE filing, RS Metal Works IPO 2015
  Confidence: 0.94
  Score contribution: +30 pts
  
  Claim: "SEBI enforcement order against promoter 2021"
  Evidence:
    Source 1: sebi.gov.in/enforcement/orders/2021
              Order No. WTM/ABC/EFD/123/2021
              Penalty: ₹2cr for disclosure violation
              Paid: within 30 days (confirmed)
  Confidence: 1.0 (government source)
  Score contribution: -25 pts
  
  [continues for all character claims...]
  
  C: CAPACITY
  ──────────────
  [All capacity claims with sources + score impacts]
  
  C: CAPITAL
  ──────────────
  [All capital claims with sources + score impacts]
  
  C: COLLATERAL
  ──────────────
  [All collateral claims with sources + score impacts]
  
  C: CONDITIONS
  ──────────────
  [All conditions claims with sources + score impacts]

COMPOUND INSIGHTS:
  [All Agent 2.5 findings with full evidence chains]

VERIFIED RESEARCH:
  [All Agent 2 findings, tiered and annotated]

UNCERTAIN FINDINGS (shown but not scored):
  [Research findings awaiting verification]

REJECTED FINDINGS (shown with rejection reason):
  [What was found but excluded and exactly why]

CONFLICTING FINDINGS (needs resolution):
  [Opposing claims, both shown]

OPEN TICKETS:
  [All unresolved conflicts awaiting human review]
The Ticketing Layer Within Evidence Package Builder
When the Evidence Package Builder encounters any of these conditions, it raises a ticket instead of making an assumption:

Ticket triggers:
  → Two sources contradict each other
  → Extraction confidence below 0.75
    for a material number
  → Research finding is unverified but material
  → DOMINANT GNN fraud signal without
    full supporting evidence chain
  → Management interview claim contradicts
    documentary evidence
  → Any finding that would change score
    by more than 20 pts if accepted vs rejected

Ticket format:
  Problem description
  Evidence for claim A (full citation)
  Evidence for claim B (full citation)
  AI reasoning about which is more likely correct
  Past precedents from RAG knowledge base
  Score impact if accepted vs rejected
  Recommended action with reasoning
  Options for human: Accept / Decline / 
                     Escalate / Custom response

Pipeline behavior:
  LOW severity tickets: pipeline continues,
    ticket resolved asynchronously
  HIGH severity tickets: pipeline pauses,
    must be resolved before Agent 3 proceeds
  CRITICAL tickets: pipeline stops completely,
    senior manager notification sent
Rejection and Fraud Storage
If the Evidence Package Builder encounters hard block conditions:

REJECTION NODE STORE (PostgreSQL):
  id, company_id, rejection_type, triggered_at,
  trigger_reasons (JSON with full evidence),
  full_pipeline_state_snapshot,
  rejection_letter_generated,
  reapplication_allowed_after,
  knowledge_base_entry_id

FRAUD INVESTIGATION STORE (PostgreSQL):
  id, company_id, fraud_type, evidence_chain,
  neo4j_subgraph_snapshot (frozen),
  ml_model_scores,
  human_verdict (pending initially),
  regulatory_report_required (PMLA/FIU-IND)
Both stores write a knowledge base entry automatically — every rejection and fraud detection becomes a precedent for future cases.

Stage 8: Ticketing Layer
The Human-AI Dialogue System
Human receives ticket in UI:
  Full problem description
  Both conflicting claims with sources
  RAG retrieves: "In 3 similar past cases..."
  Score impact shown either way
  Options shown

Human responds:
  Option A: Accept claim A
  Option B: Accept claim B
  Option C: Escalate to senior manager
  Option D: Need more information from company
  Option E: Custom free text response

AI responds to human choice:
  Confirms understanding
  Asks follow-up if the resolution
  has downstream implications
  ("You accepted this case as post-report filing.
   Should I also update the working capital 
   calculation to reflect the disputed receivable?")

Human finalizes:
  Resolution stored in PostgreSQL
  Added to ChromaDB knowledge base with:
    Pattern description
    Context (sector, company size, dispute type)
    Resolution and reasoning
    Resolver expertise level
    Outcome (to be filled when loan matures)
The RAG Learning System
Knowledge Base (ChromaDB + PostgreSQL):
  
  Every resolved ticket stored with:
    Pattern fingerprint (for similarity search)
    Resolution + reasoning
    Resolver identity + expertise
    Company context
    Outcome (updated when loan outcome known)
  
  When new ticket raised:
    RAG query: "Find resolved tickets similar to this"
    Similarity based on: pattern type + sector + amounts
    Returns: Top 3 most relevant precedents
    Shown to human: "In a similar steel sector case,
                     senior manager resolved as X
                     because Y. That loan was 
                     repaid on schedule."
  
  Over time:
    System gets better at predicting human decisions
    Precedents accumulate institutional knowledge
    Outcome tracking validates which resolutions
    were correct → strengthens those precedents
Stage 9: Agent 3 — The Recommendation Engine
What It Receives
Only the Evidence Package. Nothing else. No raw documents. No Neo4j. No Insight Store directly. Everything it needs is already organized, sourced, and scored in the package.

The Credit Score Model
INTELLI-CREDIT SCORE: 0 to 850

BANDS:
  750-850: Excellent → Approve full amount, best rate
  650-749: Good      → Approve, standard rate
  550-649: Fair      → Approve reduced, higher rate
  450-549: Poor      → Approve with strong conditions
  350-449: Very Poor → Reject, reapply in 12 months
  <350:    Default   → Permanent reject, regulatory review

HARD BLOCKS (override any score):
  Wilful defaulter    → Score capped at 200
  Active criminal case → Score capped at 150
  DSCR < 1.0x        → Score capped at 300
  NCLT active         → Score capped at 250

STARTING BASELINE: 600 (industry average)
Score moves up and down from here.
Score Module Breakdown
Every single point added or deducted has this structure:

Metric name
Value found
How it was computed (formula)
Exact source (document, page, table)
Benchmark context (industry average etc.)
Score impact
Reasoning paragraph explaining the impact
The score itself is the primary output. Loan amount and interest rate are derived from the score — they are never the AI's independent judgment:

Score → Band → Parameters:

Excellent (750-850):
  Loan: 100% of requested
  Rate: MCLR + 1.5%
  Conditions: Standard monitoring

Good (650-749):
  Loan: 85% of requested
  Rate: MCLR + 2.5%
  Conditions: Quarterly reporting

Fair (550-649):
  Loan: 65% of requested
  Rate: MCLR + 3.5%
  Conditions: Quarterly audit + collateral enhancement

Poor (450-549):
  Loan: 40% of requested
  Rate: MCLR + 5%
  Conditions: Monthly reporting + personal guarantee
              + additional collateral

MCLR as of March 2025: ~8.5%
CAM Writer
Each section generated by a dedicated LangChain chain with model tiering:

Section              Model       Input to chain
─────────────────────────────────────────────────────────────
Executive Summary    Sonnet      Score + top 3 insights + decision
Character            Haiku       Character evidence package section
Capacity             Haiku       Capacity numbers + DSCR computation
Capital              Haiku       Capital structure data
Collateral           Haiku       Asset data + coverage ratio
Conditions           Haiku       Industry + regulatory findings
Risk Flags           Sonnet      All CRITICAL + HIGH insights
Decision Rationale   Sonnet      Complete score breakdown + all reasons
Sonnet for sections judges read most carefully. Haiku for sections that are primarily number summaries.

Every sentence in the CAM references its evidence:

"Revenue has grown at an 18.2% CAGR over FY2022-24
[Annual Report FY2024, Page 43, Table 2], 
significantly above the steel sector average of 12%.
This growth has been verified against ITR filings 
[ITR FY2024 Schedule BP] confirming the revenue 
is reflected in tax declarations."
The Complete Technology Stack
Why Each Technology Was Chosen
React + TailwindCSS Frontend. React because it's the standard and has the component model needed for a multi-panel interface (upload, progress, notes, CAM viewer, ticket resolution all in one app). TailwindCSS because it produces professional UI quickly without writing CSS. Specifically not Angular because React requires far less boilerplate for a hackathon timeline.

FastAPI API backend. Two critical reasons over Flask: built-in async support (essential for WebSockets and parallel processing) and automatic OpenAPI documentation generation. Every endpoint is documented without extra work. Pydantic v2 integrates natively because FastAPI was built by the same team.

Pydantic v2 Data contracts at every boundary. The upgrade from v1 is significant: v2 is 5-50x faster for validation (rewritten in Rust), has better error messages, and supports Python type hints more completely. Every agent boundary has a Pydantic model. Bad data is caught at the boundary where it was created, not 3 steps later where the effect is mysterious.

WebSockets via FastAPI Real-time progress updates. The user sees "OCR complete... Bank statement processed... Research 60% complete..." as it happens. Without WebSockets, the user stares at a spinner for 4 minutes. With WebSockets, they're reading useful partial results within 45 seconds. This transforms the perceived experience even though the total processing time is the same.

Redis Two roles simultaneously: task queue broker for Celery and temporary cache for research results. The reason Redis handles both is that it's already running for one purpose, so using it for the other adds zero infrastructure overhead. Redis specifically over Memcached because Redis supports data structures (lists, sets, hashes, pub/sub) that Celery and our staging area both need. 7-day TTL on research results means repeated research on the same company is instant.

Celery Parallel task execution. The Python standard for distributed task queues. Specifically over alternatives like RQ (Redis Queue) because Celery has a richer feature set: task routing, retry logic with exponential backoff, task prioritization, result backend support, and a monitoring UI (Flower) that shows all running tasks in real time. During the demo, Flower shows all 8 document workers running simultaneously — visually impressive and genuinely useful.

LangGraph The orchestration engine. The entire pipeline is a LangGraph state machine. The CreditAppraisalState object passes through every node carrying the accumulated knowledge of all previous stages. Conditional edges implement the routing logic (auto-reject path, deep fraud path, human review path). The human-in-the-loop interrupt mechanism pauses the graph for ticket resolution and resumes seamlessly. LangGraph specifically over CrewAI because it gives you explicit control over every node and edge — you can show judges the exact graph and explain every decision path.

LangChain The agent framework within each node. Provides document loaders, chains, RAG retrievers, tool integrations. The reason you want LangChain on top of direct API calls: it provides tested abstractions for RAG chains, structured output parsing, conversation memory, and tool use. It also provides automatic LangSmith integration — every LangChain call is traced without any extra code.

Claude Haiku + Sonnet Model tiering. Haiku for extraction, classification, and structured data tasks. Sonnet for writing, reasoning, and complex analysis. The specific reasons for Claude over GPT-4: larger context window (fits entire annual reports in one call), stronger instruction following for structured output parsing, and better performance on financial text. Haiku specifically because at 5x lower cost and higher speed than Sonnet, using it for the 80% of LLM calls that don't need Sonnet-level quality is the difference between a 4-minute pipeline and a 12-minute pipeline.

Unstructured.io Document parsing for complex PDFs. The specific advantage over PyMuPDF: Unstructured.io understands document layout spatially — it can identify that a page has three columns and extract each column separately. For Indian annual reports which use complex multi-column layouts, headers/footers, tables spanning pages, and footnotes referencing body text, this spatial understanding is essential. PyMuPDF reads content in DOM order which destroys column structure.

Tesseract OCR Open source OCR engine. Specifically configured with page-level parallelism for A0.1. The key tuning for Indian documents: adding the rupee symbol to the character set, configuring it for mixed Hindi-English text, and using psm 6 (assume uniform block of text) for financial table pages. Why not a cloud OCR like Google Vision? Because Tesseract runs locally, has no per-page cost, and with proper pre-processing reaches comparable accuracy for printed text.

sentence-transformers/all-MiniLM-L6-v2 Local embedding model. The SBERT library's benchmark model for retrieval tasks. 384-dimensional vectors, runs on CPU in ~20ms per sentence, ~12 seconds for 600 chunks. Why this specific model? It was specifically benchmarked and trained for semantic similarity and retrieval tasks — which is exactly what our RAG system needs. Why not text-embedding-ada-002? Because 600 API calls × 500ms latency × cost per call adds up to something that a local model eliminates entirely.

ChromaDB Vector database for semantic search. Open source, runs locally as a Python package, native LangChain integration (one line to create a retriever). The specific reason over FAISS: ChromaDB has a proper client-server architecture (FAISS is just an in-memory library), supports metadata filtering (find chunks from a specific document or page range), and has a persistence layer that survives restarts.

Neo4j Community Edition Graph database. The industry standard for graph data with the most mature Python driver and the best LangChain integration. Cypher query language is expressive and well-documented. GraphRAG from Microsoft integrates with Neo4j specifically. Why not a graph extension on PostgreSQL (Apache AGE)? Because Neo4j is purpose-built for graph operations and will outperform any relational DB with graph extensions for the kinds of multi-hop traversal queries Agent 2.5 runs.

Elasticsearch 8 Full-text search and NER-tagged entity search. Four indices serving different search needs. The specific reason ES over Solr: ES has better Python client support, better REST API design, more active development for ML integration features, and the NER pipeline we need is a first-class feature in ES 8's NLP capabilities.

PostgreSQL 15 Structured relational store for FeatureObjects, Insight Store, rejection events, fraud investigations, ticket history. The specific reason over MongoDB: our schemas are well-defined and don't change. PostgreSQL's strict schema enforcement means data in these stores is always in the exact format we expect. ACID compliance means a partially written Insight Store entry never exists — it either writes completely or not at all.

DOMINANT GNN Graph neural network for circular trading and shell company detection. Pre-trained on financial transaction graphs. The specific reason: it's the most validated open-source tool for exactly this problem — anomaly detection in financial entity graphs. Available via PyTorch Geometric. Fine-tuned on SEBI enforcement order descriptions which provide labeled examples of exactly the patterns we're looking for.

Isolation Forest Unsupervised tabular anomaly detection. scikit-learn implementation. No labeled training data needed — it works by learning the distribution of normal data and identifying what doesn't fit. The specific reason over one-class SVM or DBSCAN: Isolation Forest was specifically designed and benchmarked for anomaly detection and outperforms alternatives on tabular financial data in most benchmarks.

FinBERT (ProsusAI) Financial text analysis. Available on HuggingFace. Pre-trained on financial news, earnings calls, and financial reports. The specific reason over vanilla BERT: the pre-training domain matches our use case exactly. FinBERT understands that "notwithstanding temporary headwinds" is a negative signal even though every individual word could be neutral.

spaCy + GLiNER Named Entity Recognition. spaCy for standard entities (dates, amounts, organizations). GLiNER for zero-shot entity recognition that works without fine-tuning. The specific reason for GLiNER: it can recognize entity types that weren't in its training data — Indian court names, Indian regulatory body names, Indian company name patterns — without needing to collect labeled training examples.

Tavily API Primary web search for AI agents. Purpose-built for LLM usage — returns clean structured text, supports domain filtering, has built-in relevance scoring. Native LangChain integration means it's one line of code to add as an agent tool.

Exa Neural Search Semantic web search. Neural indexing means Exa finds conceptually related content — the promoter's other company default story even if the current company is never mentioned. This is the capability that makes the "connect the dots" research possible at the web layer.

SerpAPI Google search wrapper. The specific reason: Google has the most comprehensive index of Indian business news. No other search API covers Economic Times, Business Standard, Mint, and Financial Express as thoroughly as Google. SerpAPI wraps this with a clean JSON API.

BeautifulSoup + Selenium Custom Indian government portal scrapers. BeautifulSoup for static HTML pages. Selenium for dynamic pages that render via JavaScript. The five scrapers (MCA21, NJDG, SEBI, RBI defaulters, GSTIN) are the most uniquely valuable components in the entire system because no API or third-party service provides this data in a structured, query-able form.

LangSmith Complete observability for the entire system. Every LLM call, every agent decision, every tool use is automatically traced and stored. The demo value is significant — you can show judges a dashboard where they click through every decision the AI made. Why LangSmith over alternatives: it was built by the LangChain team specifically for this purpose and has zero-config integration with LangChain and LangGraph.

python-docx CAM document generation. Produces the final Word document that a real banker would read. The specific reason over ReportLab (which produces PDFs): Word format is the industry standard for credit appraisal memos in Indian banking. It can be edited after generation, which bankers prefer. python-docx gives programmatic control over every formatting element.

Docker Compose Infrastructure orchestration for development and demo. Single command spins up all eight services (Redis, PostgreSQL, Elasticsearch, Neo4j, ChromaDB, FastAPI, Celery workers, Flower). Every service runs in an isolated container. Works on any machine. The demo can be set up on a laptop in a conference room with one command. Why not Kubernetes: overkill for hackathon. K8s requires cluster setup, manifest files, ingress configuration — days of work for zero visible demo benefit.

Microsoft GraphRAG Multi-hop reasoning over the knowledge graph. Takes the Neo4j graph and creates hierarchical summaries that the LLM can use for reasoning without seeing raw graph data. The specific capability: it can answer questions like "what are the major risk communities in this graph?" by retrieving the relevant subgraph context automatically.

The New Features Added From PS Review
These were missing in the original A0 and A0.1 design but identified when reviewing the problem statement carefully:

Board Meeting Minutes — Now explicitly handled by Worker 6 with dedicated extraction for governance signals, related party approval cross-referencing, and director concern pattern detection.

Shareholding Pattern — Now handled by Worker 7 with specific pledge ratio analysis, cross-holding detection, and promoter selling trend analysis.

Rating Agency Reports — Now handled by Worker 8 with rating history tracking, downgrade detection, and rating agency language extraction for the CAM.

CIBIL Commercial — Handled as an input field in the UI. When provided, integrated into Character module scoring. When not provided, noted as absent with confidence reduction. The scoring model is designed to incorporate it.

Databricks — Represented as the data source layer in the architecture. A mock Databricks connector module reads from local files with the same interface as a real Databricks connection. Easy to swap to real Databricks in production.

ITR Deep Parsing — Worker 4 now explicitly extracts all ITR schedules and runs ITR-vs-Annual-Report divergence computation.

Management Interview Structure — Structured input form in the UI with sections matching the 5 Cs. AI compares interview responses against documentary evidence and scores management credibility.

GSTR-2A vs GSTR-3B Reconciliation — Worker 3 explicitly computes this discrepancy. It's in the evaluation criteria and judges will look for it specifically.

Agent 0.5 Consolidator — The parallel worker output merging problem is now explicitly solved.

Agent 1.5 Organizer — Data organization before research is now an explicit pipeline stage.

Rejection and Fraud Node Storage — Both now have explicit PostgreSQL tables with full evidence snapshots.

Credit Score (0-850) — Primary output is a score, not an approve/reject. The recommendation is derived from the score with transparent logic.

Ticketing Layer with RAG Learning — Every conflict or uncertainty raises a ticket. Human resolutions feed into a knowledge base. Outcomes are tracked to validate resolutions over time.

Synthesized comprehensive architecture integrating decision logging and real-time agent visualization
Synthesized comprehensive architecture integrating decision logging and real-time agent visualization
This is the final, complete architecture. Let me cover everything from scratch in one definitive discussion — every agent, every layer, every tech, the decision store, and the live thinking chatbot.

The Core Philosophy — One Final Statement
A0.1 is built on four principles:

1. DATA BEFORE LLM
   Every piece of data is organized, verified,
   and sourced BEFORE any LLM sees it.
   LLMs write and reason. They never hunt for data.

2. SINGLE RESPONSIBILITY
   Every agent does exactly one job.
   Every database stores exactly one type of thing.
   No component does two things.

3. NOTHING IS LOST
   Every decision — approve, reject, fraud, borderline —
   is stored with full evidence and reasoning.
   Every AI thought is logged and shown.
   Every human resolution is recorded and learned from.

4. FULL TRANSPARENCY
   The credit officer sees exactly what the AI read,
   what it thought, what it accepted, what it rejected,
   and why — in real time, in plain language.

The Live Thinking Chatbot — Complete Design
This is the most important new feature for the demo and for transparency. Let me explain it completely.

What It Is
A persistent chat panel in the UI that shows the AI's complete internal monologue in real time. Not a summary. Not logs. The actual reasoning — what document the agent is reading, what text it found, what it decided to do with it, and why. Every agent is named. Every document is named. Every decision is shown with its outcome.

Why It Exists
Three reasons:

1. TRANSPARENCY
   The credit officer is not a passive recipient
   of an AI decision. They are an active participant
   who can see exactly what the AI read and thought.
   If the AI read something wrong, the officer
   catches it immediately.

2. TRUST
   A black box AI making lending decisions will
   never be trusted by bankers. A system that
   narrates its reasoning like an expert colleague
   explaining their thought process builds trust
   naturally.

3. DEMO IMPACT
   Judges watching the AI think in real time —
   naming documents, quoting text, explaining
   decisions — is the most compelling demonstration
   of explainability possible.
The Thinking Event Architecture
Every agent in the system emits structured Thinking Events throughout its processing. These events are published to a Redis Pub/Sub channel. A WebSocket server subscribes to this channel and pushes events to the UI in real time.

THINKING EVENT STRUCTURE:

ThinkingEvent {
  event_id:      UUID
  timestamp:     ISO datetime
  session_id:    "assessment_XYZ_Steel_001"
  
  agent_name:    "Agent 1.5 — The Organizer"
  agent_stage:   "COMPUTING_METRICS"
  
  event_type:    READ | FOUND | COMPUTED | ACCEPTED |
                 REJECTED | FLAGGED | DECIDED |
                 QUESTIONING | CONNECTING | CONCLUDING
  
  document_name: "Annual Report FY2024.pdf"
  page_number:   43
  
  content:       Full text the agent is processing
                 (the actual words from the document
                 or the actual web result)
  
  extracted:     What the agent pulled from this content
  
  decision:      ACCEPTED | REJECTED | FLAGGED | UNCERTAIN
  decision_reason: Why this decision was made
  
  score_impact:  +7 pts (if applicable)
  confidence:    0.94
  
  links_to:      [other event IDs this connects to]
}

              as on the date of this report"

     Tagged as: CHARACTER > Litigation Disclosure
     ⚠️ Cross-verification queued

   → Page 89 — Related Party Transactions
     Reading: "Transactions with related parties
              during the year: 2 entities"
     Found: Supplier A — ₹12cr transactions
            Supplier B — ₹9.8cr transactions
     Decision: ✅ ACCEPTED

     Tagged as: CAPITAL > Related Party Transactions

     D/E 2.10x:               -5 pts
     Existing loan obligations:-10 pts
     Net worth adequate:      +10 pts
     Subtotal: -5
   
   MODULE: COLLATERAL
     Coverage 1.7x:           +25 pts
     Quality of asset:        +10 pts
     Subtotal: +35
   
   MODULE: CONDITIONS
     Order book ₹280cr:       +15 pts
     Sector headwinds:        -10 pts
     RBI not defaulter:       +10 pts
     Subtotal: +15
   
   COMPOUND INSIGHTS:
     Cascade risk (Greenfield): -50 pts
     Shell company network:     -60 pts
     Temporal deterioration:    -20 pts
   
   ─────────────────────────────────────
   FINAL CALCULATION:
     600 (baseline) + 42 - 80 - 5 + 35 + 15 - 50 - 60 - 20
     = 477
   
   INTELLI-CREDIT SCORE: 477
   BAND: POOR (450-549)
   
   Derived recommendation:
     Loan amount: 40% of ₹50cr requested = ₹20cr
     Interest rate: MCLR + 5% = 13.5%
     Conditions: Monthly reporting, personal guarantee,
                 complete collateral over factory,
                 compliance review of RPT issue first
   
   Generating CAM document...
   ✅ CAM complete.

The Universal Decision Store — Complete Design
Every single outcome is stored. Approvals, rejections, fraud detections, borderline cases, overturned decisions — everything. This is a complete institutional memory system.

Schema Design
TABLE: assessments (master record for every assessment)

How All Stores Connect
SINGLE ASSESSMENT SESSION LINKS EVERYTHING:

assessment (session_id: IC-2025-0847)
    │
    ├──▶ score_breakdown (12 score entries)
    │         each with document + page + formula
    │
    ├──▶ findings_store (47 research + 17 compound)
    │         each with source + decision + reason
    │
    ├──▶ tickets (3 tickets)
    │         each with both claims + resolution
    │         → feeds knowledge_base
    │
    ├──▶ thinking_events (847 events logged)
    │         complete AI thought record
    │         shown in live chatbot
    │
    └──▶ decision_outcomes (filled after loan matures)
              validates the assessment retrospectively

APPROVED ASSESSMENT:
  All of the above stored
  + CAM document
  + Score report
  + LangSmith trace
  + Loan terms explicitly recorded
  + Outcome tracked when loan matures

REJECTED ASSESSMENT:
  All of the above stored
  + Rejection letter generated
  + Reapplication date recorded
  + Fraud report (if fraud detected)
  + Regulatory referral (if required)

BORDERLINE (escalated):
  All of the above stored
  + Escalation record
  + Senior manager review record
  + Committee vote record (if applicable)
  + Final override decision with justification
The RAG Knowledge Base
Every resolved ticket and every matured loan outcome feeds the knowledge base. This is what makes the system smarter over time without retraining:

KNOWLEDGE BASE ENTRY (created on ticket resolution):

pattern_type:       RPT_UNDISCLOSED
sector:             MANUFACTURING_STEEL
company_size:       MID (₹50-200cr revenue)

situation:          "Board minutes showed 5 RPTs.
                    Annual report showed 2.
                    Undisclosed value: ₹19.2cr"

resolution:         CONFIRMED CONCEALMENT
resolution_reason:  "Same year, same board.
                    No timing explanation possible.
                    Penalty applied."

resolved_by:        Senior Credit Manager
expertise:          12 years, steel sector specialist
score_applied:      -45 pts

outcome:            (filled 18 months later)
  "Loan was conditionally approved at ₹20cr.
   Company restructured 14 months later.
   RPT findings were validated by CA audit.
   Assessment was correct."

validated_signal:   true
precedent_weight:   HIGH (outcome confirmed)
tags:               [rpt_concealment, board_minutes_gap,
                     steel_sector, mid_size, confirmed]
When a new ticket about undisclosed RPTs is raised in the future, the system retrieves this precedent and tells the credit officer exactly what happened last time, who resolved it, how, and what the outcome was.

The Thinking Event System — Technical Design
How Events Flow From Agent to Chatbot
AGENT (any stage)
  │
  │ agent.emit(ThinkingEvent(
  │   agent_name = "Agent 2 — Research Agent",
  │   event_type = "FOUND",
  │   document_name = "MCA21 Portal",
  │   content = "DIN 01234567 found as director of Supplier A",
  │   decision = "FLAGGED",
  │   decision_reason = "Promoter controlling supplier"
  │ ))
  │
  ▼
Redis Pub/Sub Channel: "thinking:{session_id}"
  │
  ▼
WebSocket Server (FastAPI)
  Subscribed to this channel
  Receives event immediately
  │
  ▼
WebSocket Push to all connected UI clients
  for this session
  │
  ▼
React Live Chatbot Component
  Appends new message to feed
  Formats with agent name, icon, color
  Shows document name, page, content
  Shows decision with color coding:
    ✅ Green = Accepted
    ⚠️ Yellow = Flagged
    🚨 Red = Critical flag
    ❌ Rejected = Crossed out
    💬 Questioning = AI asking
  Scrolls to latest event
  Full event stored in thinking_events table
Event Types and Their Display
READ         → "Agent 1.5 is reading Annual Report pg 43"
FOUND        → "Found: Revenue ₹124.5cr"
COMPUTED     → "Computed: DSCR = 18200/12700 = 1.43x"
ACCEPTED     ✅ "Accepted: Revenue figure, confidence 0.97"
REJECTED     ❌ "Rejected: Blog post, unverifiable source"
FLAGGED      ⚠️ "Flagged: ITC claimed > ITC available"
CRITICAL     🚨 "Critical: 3 undisclosed related parties"
CONNECTING   🔗 "Connecting: Greenfield NCLT → revenue loss"
CONCLUDING   💡 "Conclusion: DSCR drops to 0.88x in stress"
QUESTIONING  💬 "Agent 2.5 asks: Should I include Priya Shah
                 transactions in the circular trading analysis?"
DECIDED      ✅ "Score module CAPACITY: +42 pts"

  [etc.]

User uploads 8 documents + enters management interview
                    │
                    ▼

Celery task per document created → Redis queued
                    │
                    ▼
8 Workers fire simultaneously

                    │
                    ▼

Waits for all → Conflict detection →

                    │

           Complete           Tickets raised

               │

Verification Engine

               │
               ▼

5 passes over complete Neo4j

Emits THINKING EVENTS per reasoning step
               │
               ▼

               │
        ┌──────┴─────────────┐
        │                    │
    Tickets             No tickets
    resolved by         or LOW only
    human                    │
        │                    │

               │

assessment + score_breakdown + findings_store
+ tickets + thinking_events

LangSmith trace archived

               │
               ▼
